I’m checking two things in parallel: what your current script/output actually did, and what current best practice says about choosing variable features and PCs for large, diverse scRNA-seq. Then I’ll turn that into concrete figures/legends and a decision rule you can use.

I found your pipeline bundle, including the current 07_integration_sensitivity.r, the older version, and the generated Harmony figures/logs. Next I’m pulling out the exact parts that should become parameter-sweep plots so you can choose HVGs/PCs based on evidence instead of guessing.

Thought for 1m 16s

Yes — 4,000 HVGs is a defensible starting point for your placenta dataset. For a highly heterogeneous tissue with many lineages and states, 2,000 can be a little conservative, especially if you want to preserve rarer stromal/immune/trophoblast structure. Seurat’s default is 2,000, but that is a default, not a rule. Their docs describe FindVariableFeatures() as selecting genes with high variance after accounting for the mean–variance relationship, and ElbowPlot() as the fast first-pass way to choose PCs; JackStraw is available when you want a more formal PC significance assessment, though it is heavier.

From the files you uploaded, I checked your current 07_integration_sensitivity.r and the log. The current script is still a single-run setup using 4,000 HVGs and 50 PCs, and the log shows the earlier crash was std::bad_alloc, so the real issue is not that 4,000 is “wrong,” but that you need a parameter-testing workflow and a safer fallback when memory is tight. Also, a few older uploaded files in this chat have expired, so if you want me to inspect any earlier files again, re-upload them.

My recommendation

Keep 4,000 HVGs as the anchor candidate, but do not hard-code it as truth yet.
For your data, I would compare:

HVGs: 2000, 3000, 4000, 5000

PCs: 20, 30, 40, 50, 60

Then choose the smallest setting that still preserves:

placental major lineages cleanly

donor mixing after Harmony

infection/time structure not erased

rare but biologically relevant populations not collapsing

That is more publication-grade than arguing from intuition alone. Single-cell best-practice guides explicitly frame feature selection as dataset-dependent, with common workflows often using about 500–2,000 genes, but they also emphasize that the goal is to keep informative biological variation and not uncritically inherit defaults.

Best-practice way to decide HVGs

Use three layers of evidence.

1. Stability of biological structure

Run the same workflow across HVG counts and ask:

do vCTB / EVT / SCT / fibroblast / endothelial / immune compartments remain distinct?

does FIB2 stay coherent?

do infection/time shifts remain visible?

do rare states disappear when HVGs are too low?

If 2,000 loses rare structure and 4,000–5,000 recovers it, that supports the larger number.

2. Sensitivity to technical noise

Too many HVGs can start pulling in noisy genes. Look for:

donor-driven separation before Harmony

over-correction after Harmony

unstable cluster identities across runs

UMAPs that become more fragmented without adding interpretable biology

If 5,000 adds mostly instability and 4,000 is stable, 4,000 wins.

3. Downstream robustness

Pick the HVG count that gives similar conclusions across neighboring settings.
If your key conclusions hold at 3,000, 4,000, and 5,000, then 4,000 is easy to defend.

Best-practice way to decide number of PCs

Do not pick 30 or 50 just because it is common. Use:

ElbowPlot for the initial break point

JackStraw on a smaller representative subset if you want a more formal support plot for PC significance

biological interpretability of late PCs

stability of UMAP/clustering across PC ranges

For your dataset, I would expect a plausible final choice around 30–50 PCs, but I would justify it by showing:

elbow near that range

late PCs after that point are mostly weak or donor/noise-driven

main biological conclusions do not materially change between, say, 40 and 50 PCs

What figures you should make

I would add a small “parameter sensitivity” section with 4 figure groups.

Figure A. HVG sweep summary

Panels:

number of HVGs tested

UMAP by cell type for each HVG setting

UMAP by donor for each HVG setting

UMAP by infection/condition for each HVG setting

Legend idea:
“Parameter sensitivity to highly variable feature selection. Increasing HVGs improved capture of lineage/state diversity up to an intermediate range, after which added features contributed limited additional biological resolution.”

Figure B. PC sweep summary

Panels:

elbow plot

optional JackStraw plot on a subset

UMAPs using 20, 30, 40, 50, 60 PCs

donor/infection overlays for each

Legend idea:
“Principal component sensitivity analysis. We selected the smallest PC range that preserved major placental lineages and infection-associated structure while avoiding excessive incorporation of weak higher-order technical axes.”

Figure C. Quantitative score plot

One panel per metric across HVG × PC combinations:

donor mixing score after Harmony

cell-type conservation score

infection/stage separation retention

optional cluster stability / ARI

This is the most convincing figure for reviewer-proofing.

Figure D. Chosen setting, final diagnostic

For the chosen combo:

Harmony UMAP by cell type

Harmony UMAP by donor

Harmony UMAP by infection

Harmony UMAP by stage/condition

Decision rule I would actually use

Choose the parameter set that:

preserves all major expected placenta compartments

preserves your biologically critical compartments/states:

vCTB-related susceptibility axis

FIB2 metabolic niche

immune components

improves donor mixing after Harmony

does not erase infection/time biology

is stable across neighboring parameter values

For your project, I would probably favor something like:

HVGs = 4000

PCs = 40 or 50

unless the sweep shows 5000 meaningfully improves rare states without introducing noise, or 3000 performs equivalently.

Important point about memory

The solution is not “must downsample.”
A better rule is:

try full object first

if FindVariableFeatures or scaling fails, fall back to a working copy

keep the full object untouched

Also, if memory is the choke point, consider:

testing the parameter sweep on a stratified subset

then rerunning the winning settings on the full object if feasible

That way, downsampling is only for parameter tuning, not for the final biological conclusion.

What I would add to your pipeline

I would add a new script, something like 07b_parameter_sensitivity.R, that:

loops over HVGs = 2000, 3000, 4000, 5000

loops over PCs = 20, 30, 40, 50, 60

computes PCA, UMAP, Harmony

saves:

elbow plots

UMAPs

a summary table of metrics

writes legends automatically

A minimal metric table could include:

n_hvg

n_pc

variance_explained_pc1_10

variance_explained_pc1_20

celltype_neighbor_purity

donor_mixing_score

condition_separation_score

Bottom line

I would not abandon 4,000 HVGs.
I would treat it as your leading candidate and build a sensitivity figure set around it.

My current best recommendation is:

start with 4000 HVGs

test 2000 / 3000 / 4000 / 5000

test 20 / 30 / 40 / 50 / 60 PCs

choose the smallest setting that preserves biological resolution and does not over-correct infection/time structure

That is much easier to defend in a paper than “we used 4000 because the tissue is diverse,” even though that intuition is reasonable.

Thought for 33s

Yes — with ~100 GB free RAM out of 128 GB, you should be able to test 4,000 HVGs on the full object and likely a modest parameter sweep too, though JackStraw is still expensive enough that I would run it on a representative subset rather than the full 159k cells. Seurat’s docs position FindVariableFeatures() as the step that identifies informative genes after accounting for the mean–variance relationship, ElbowPlot() as the quick heuristic for PC choice, and JackStraw() as the more formal but heavier significance test for PCs. Harmony also expects PCA to already exist and then uses those embeddings downstream.

I also checked the script bundle you uploaded. Your current 07_integration_sensitivity.r is now running the full object with 4,000 HVGs and 50 PCs, and the earlier failure in the log is std::bad_alloc, so the right move is not automatic downsampling, but a controlled sensitivity script that tests HVGs and PCs systematically and only falls back to a subset for the expensive formal diagnostics. A few older files from earlier in the chat have expired on my side, so if you want me to inspect any of those again, re-upload them.

Here is the version I would use next: a new script that sweeps HVGs and PCs, saves figures, writes legends, and produces a score table so you can choose the best setting based on evidence.

source("R/config.R")
source("R/helpers_io.R")

suppressPackageStartupMessages({
  library(Seurat)
  library(dplyr)
  library(ggplot2)
  library(qs)
  library(patchwork)
})

# -----------------------------
# SETTINGS
# -----------------------------
log_file <- file.path(CFG$dirs$logs, "pipeline.log")
out_tbl  <- file.path(CFG$dirs$tables, "integration_param_sweep_summary.csv")

# Main grid to test
hvg_grid <- c(2000, 3000, 4000, 5000)
pc_grid  <- c(20, 30, 40, 50, 60)

# Optional subset for heavy formal diagnostics
jackstraw_cells <- 30000
seed <- 42

# -----------------------------
# HELPERS
# -----------------------------
run_harmony_compat <- function(seu_obj, batch_col, dims = 1:30, reduction_save = "harmony") {
  fn <- get("RunHarmony", envir = asNamespace("harmony"))
  fn_formals <- names(formals(fn))

  args <- list(
    object = seu_obj,
    group.by.vars = batch_col,
    verbose = FALSE
  )

  if ("reduction" %in% fn_formals) {
    args$reduction <- "pca"
  } else if ("reduction.use" %in% fn_formals) {
    args$reduction.use <- "pca"
  }

  if ("dims.use" %in% fn_formals) args$dims.use <- dims
  if ("assay.use" %in% fn_formals) args$assay.use <- "RNA"
  if ("reduction.save" %in% fn_formals) args$reduction.save <- reduction_save

  do.call(fn, args)
}

safe_dimplot <- function(seu_obj, reduction, group_by, title_txt) {
  if (!reduction %in% names(seu_obj@reductions)) return(NULL)
  if (!group_by %in% colnames(seu_obj@meta.data)) return(NULL)

  DimPlot(seu_obj, reduction = reduction, group.by = group_by, raster = TRUE) +
    ggtitle(title_txt)
}

save_if_not_null <- function(path, p, w = 10, h = 8) {
  if (!is.null(p)) save_plot(path, p, w = w, h = h)
}

downsample_stratified <- function(seu_obj, max_cells = 30000, seed = 42) {
  n <- ncol(seu_obj)
  if (n <= max_cells) return(seu_obj)

  set.seed(seed)
  md <- seu_obj@meta.data

  key <- if (all(c(CFG$cols$cell_type, CFG$cols$donor_id) %in% colnames(md))) {
    paste(md[[CFG$cols$cell_type]], md[[CFG$cols$donor_id]], sep = "__")
  } else {
    rep("all", n)
  }

  idx_by_group <- split(seq_len(n), key)
  group_sizes <- vapply(idx_by_group, length, integer(1))

  target <- round(group_sizes / sum(group_sizes) * max_cells)
  target[target == 0] <- 1L
  target <- pmin(target, group_sizes)

  diff_n <- sum(target) - max_cells
  if (diff_n > 0) {
    reducible <- which(target > 1)
    while (diff_n > 0 && length(reducible) > 0) {
      j <- sample(reducible, 1)
      target[j] <- target[j] - 1L
      diff_n <- diff_n - 1L
      reducible <- which(target > 1)
    }
  } else if (diff_n < 0) {
    expandable <- which(target < group_sizes)
    while (diff_n < 0 && length(expandable) > 0) {
      j <- sample(expandable, 1)
      target[j] <- target[j] + 1L
      diff_n <- diff_n + 1L
      expandable <- which(target < group_sizes)
    }
  }

  keep <- unlist(
    Map(function(ix, k) sample(ix, size = k), idx_by_group, target),
    use.names = FALSE
  )

  subset(seu_obj, cells = colnames(seu_obj)[sort(keep)])
}

neighbor_purity <- function(emb, labels, k = 15) {
  # emb: matrix cells x dims
  # labels: vector
  if (nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)

  d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
  diag(d) <- Inf
  nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])

  if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)

  pur <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
    mean(labels[nn[, i]] == labels[i], na.rm = TRUE)
  })
  mean(pur, na.rm = TRUE)
}

mixing_score <- function(emb, batch, k = 15) {
  # higher = more donor mixing
  if (nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)

  d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
  diag(d) <- Inf
  nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])

  if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)

  mix <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
    mean(batch[nn[, i]] != batch[i], na.rm = TRUE)
  })
  mean(mix, na.rm = TRUE)
}

condition_neighbor_enrichment <- function(emb, cond, k = 15) {
  # higher = local condition coherence
  if (length(unique(cond)) < 2 || nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)

  d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
  diag(d) <- Inf
  nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])

  if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)

  score <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
    mean(cond[nn[, i]] == cond[i], na.rm = TRUE)
  })
  mean(score, na.rm = TRUE)
}

prep_pca <- function(obj, nfeatures, npcs = 60) {
  DefaultAssay(obj) <- "RNA"
  obj <- NormalizeData(obj, verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- FindVariableFeatures(obj, nfeatures = nfeatures, verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- ScaleData(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- RunPCA(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), npcs = npcs, verbose = FALSE)
  obj
}

pc_var_table <- function(seu_obj) {
  stdev <- seu_obj[["pca"]]@stdev
  data.frame(
    PC = seq_along(stdev),
    stdev = stdev,
    var_explained = (stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2),
    cumvar = cumsum((stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2))
  )
}

# -----------------------------
# LOAD OBJECT
# -----------------------------
log_msg("07b_parameter_sensitivity starting.", log_file = log_file)

seu <- qs::qread(file.path(CFG$dirs$objects, "seu_with_scores.qs"))
DefaultAssay(seu) <- "RNA"

batch_col <- CFG$cols$donor_id
if (!batch_col %in% colnames(seu@meta.data)) {
  stop("Missing donor/batch column: ", batch_col)
}

if (!"condition" %in% colnames(seu@meta.data) &&
    all(c(CFG$cols$infection, CFG$cols$hpi) %in% colnames(seu@meta.data))) {
  seu$condition <- paste0(seu[[CFG$cols$infection]][,1], "_", seu[[CFG$cols$hpi]][,1])
}

# representative subset for formal/fast diagnostics if needed
seu_js <- downsample_stratified(seu, max_cells = jackstraw_cells, seed = seed)

summary_rows <- list()

# -----------------------------
# PARAMETER SWEEP
# -----------------------------
for (n_hvg in hvg_grid) {
  log_msg("Starting HVG setting: ", n_hvg, log_file = log_file)

  obj <- prep_pca(seu, nfeatures = n_hvg, npcs = max(pc_grid))
  pca_tbl <- pc_var_table(obj)

  # Save elbow plot and variance table for each HVG setting
  p_elbow <- ElbowPlot(obj, ndims = max(pc_grid), reduction = "pca") +
    ggtitle(paste0("ElbowPlot | HVGs=", n_hvg))
  save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_Elbow_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
            p_elbow, w = 9, h = 6)

  write.csv(
    pca_tbl,
    file.path(CFG$dirs$tables, paste0("PCA_variance_HVG", n_hvg, ".csv")),
    row.names = FALSE
  )

  # Optional variable feature plot
  p_vf <- VariableFeaturePlot(obj) +
    ggtitle(paste0("VariableFeaturePlot | HVGs=", n_hvg))
  save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_VariableFeatures_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
            p_vf, w = 9, h = 6)

  for (n_pc in pc_grid) {
    log_msg("Running HVG=", n_hvg, " | PCs=", n_pc, log_file = log_file)

    tmp <- obj

    # Non-integrated UMAP
    tmp <- RunUMAP(
      tmp,
      dims = 1:n_pc,
      reduction = "pca",
      reduction.name = paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc),
      n.neighbors = 30,
      min.dist = 0.3,
      verbose = FALSE
    )

    # Harmony + Harmony UMAP
    if (requireNamespace("harmony", quietly = TRUE)) {
      harm_name <- paste0("harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc)

      tmp <- run_harmony_compat(
        seu_obj = tmp,
        batch_col = batch_col,
        dims = 1:n_pc,
        reduction_save = harm_name
      )

      tmp <- RunUMAP(
        tmp,
        dims = 1:n_pc,
        reduction = harm_name,
        reduction.name = paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc),
        n.neighbors = 30,
        min.dist = 0.3,
        verbose = FALSE
      )
    }

    # Figure panel for this combination
    p1 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$cell_type,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | cell type | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p2 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), batch_col,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | donor | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p3 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$infection,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | infection | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p4 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), "condition",
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | condition | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))

    if (!is.null(p1) && !is.null(p2) && !is.null(p3) && !is.null(p4)) {
      panel <- (p1 | p2) / (p3 | p4)
      save_plot(
        file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_RNA_HVG", n_hvg, "_PC", n_pc, ".pdf")),
        panel, w = 16, h = 12
      )
    }

    if (paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc) %in% names(tmp@reductions)) {
      h1 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$cell_type,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | cell type | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h2 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), batch_col,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | donor | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h3 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$infection,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | infection | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h4 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), "condition",
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | condition | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))

      if (!is.null(h1) && !is.null(h2) && !is.null(h3) && !is.null(h4)) {
        hpanel <- (h1 | h2) / (h3 | h4)
        save_plot(
          file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_Harmony_HVG", n_hvg, "_PC", n_pc, ".pdf")),
          hpanel, w = 16, h = 12
        )
      }
    }

    # Quantitative metrics on embeddings
    emb_pca <- Embeddings(tmp, "pca")[, 1:n_pc, drop = FALSE]
    ct_lab <- tmp@meta.data[[CFG$cols$cell_type]]
    donor_lab <- tmp@meta.data[[batch_col]]
    cond_lab <- if ("condition" %in% colnames(tmp@meta.data)) tmp@meta.data$condition else rep(NA, ncol(tmp))

    pca_celltype_purity <- neighbor_purity(emb_pca, ct_lab, k = 15)
    pca_donor_mixing <- mixing_score(emb_pca, donor_lab, k = 15)
    pca_condition_local <- condition_neighbor_enrichment(emb_pca, cond_lab, k = 15)

    harm_celltype_purity <- NA_real_
    harm_donor_mixing <- NA_real_
    harm_condition_local <- NA_real_

    harm_name <- paste0("harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc)
    if (harm_name %in% names(tmp@reductions)) {
      emb_h <- Embeddings(tmp, harm_name)[, 1:n_pc, drop = FALSE]
      harm_celltype_purity <- neighbor_purity(emb_h, ct_lab, k = 15)
      harm_donor_mixing <- mixing_score(emb_h, donor_lab, k = 15)
      harm_condition_local <- condition_neighbor_enrichment(emb_h, cond_lab, k = 15)
    }

    summary_rows[[length(summary_rows) + 1]] <- data.frame(
      n_cells = ncol(tmp),
      hvg = n_hvg,
      pcs = n_pc,
      pca_var_pc1_10 = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(10, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_var_pc1_20 = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(20, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_var_pc1_n = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(n_pc, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_celltype_purity = pca_celltype_purity,
      pca_donor_mixing = pca_donor_mixing,
      pca_condition_local = pca_condition_local,
      harmony_celltype_purity = harm_celltype_purity,
      harmony_donor_mixing = harm_donor_mixing,
      harmony_condition_local = harm_condition_local
    )
  }

  # Optional JackStraw on subset only for this HVG setting
  log_msg("Running JackStraw subset diagnostic for HVG=", n_hvg, log_file = log_file)
  js_obj <- prep_pca(seu_js, nfeatures = n_hvg, npcs = max(pc_grid))
  js_obj <- JackStraw(js_obj, dims = max(pc_grid), num.replicate = 100, verbose = FALSE)
  js_obj <- ScoreJackStraw(js_obj, dims = 1:max(pc_grid))

  p_js <- JackStrawPlot(js_obj, dims = 1:20) +
    ggtitle(paste0("JackStraw subset | HVGs=", n_hvg))
  save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_JackStraw_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
            p_js, w = 12, h = 8)
}

summary_df <- bind_rows(summary_rows)
write.csv(summary_df, out_tbl, row.names = FALSE)

# Summary score plots
p_mix <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = pcs, y = harmony_donor_mixing, color = factor(hvg), group = hvg)) +
  geom_line() + geom_point() +
  labs(title = "Harmony donor mixing across HVG/PC settings", color = "HVGs") +
  theme_bw()

p_purity <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = pcs, y = harmony_celltype_purity, color = factor(hvg), group = hvg)) +
  geom_line() + geom_point() +
  labs(title = "Harmony cell-type purity across HVG/PC settings", color = "HVGs") +
  theme_bw()

p_cond <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = pcs, y = harmony_condition_local, color = factor(hvg), group = hvg)) +
  geom_line() + geom_point() +
  labs(title = "Harmony condition-locality across HVG/PC settings", color = "HVGs") +
  theme_bw()

save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_donor_mixing.pdf"), p_mix, w = 10, h = 7)
save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_celltype_purity.pdf"), p_purity, w = 10, h = 7)
save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_condition_locality.pdf"), p_cond, w = 10, h = 7)

write_legend(
  "FigParam", "Parameter sensitivity for HVGs and PCs",
  hypothesis = "The chosen dimensionality settings should preserve major placental lineages and infection/time-associated biology while minimizing donor-driven structure after batch correction.",
  methods = paste(
    "Tested HVGs =", paste(hvg_grid, collapse = ","),
    "; tested PCs =", paste(pc_grid, collapse = ","),
    ". For each setting, we ran PCA, non-integrated UMAP, Harmony integration by donor, Harmony UMAP, and subset-based JackStraw diagnostics."
  ),
  readout = paste(
    "Preferred settings show strong cell-type coherence, improved donor mixing after Harmony,",
    "and retention of condition-associated local structure without evidence of over-correction."
  ),
  interpretation_template = paste(
    "- Choose the smallest PC range that stabilizes biological structure.",
    "\n- Favor HVG settings that preserve rare/important populations without fragmenting embeddings.",
    "\n- If donor mixing improves but infection/stage structure collapses, integration is likely too aggressive.",
    "\n- If larger HVG settings do not improve biological resolution, prefer the simpler setting."
  ),
  outfile = file.path(CFG$dirs$legends, "FigParam_legend.md")
)

log_msg("07b_parameter_sensitivity done.", log_file = log_file)
How I’d use it with your machine

With your RAM, I would start exactly like this:

HVGs: 2000, 3000, 4000, 5000

PCs: 20, 30, 40, 50, 60

full object for PCA/UMAP/Harmony

JackStraw only on the 30k stratified subset

That is a sensible compromise because ElbowPlot is explicitly the quick first-pass PC diagnostic, while JackStraw is the heavier formal significance test.

What to pick as the likely winner

Before even running the sweep, my best guess for your placenta data is still:

HVGs = 4000

PCs = 40 or 50

That fits your biological complexity and is easy to defend if the sweep shows similar or better preservation of major lineages, FIB2 coherence, and infection/time structure than 2000–3000 HVGs, without obvious fragmentation at 5000. Seurat’s own workflow materials present elbow-based PC selection as a heuristic tied to where additional PCs stop adding meaningful structure, rather than a universal fixed number.

A very important practical note

Your current 07_integration_sensitivity.r still has duplicated normalization lines and is only a single-setting run. I would leave it as the simple production figure script and add the code above as a new script such as:

07b_parameter_sensitivity.R

Then:

run 07b to choose the settings

lock the chosen settings

keep 07 as the clean “final integrated diagnostic figure” step

That keeps the pipeline organized and reviewer-friendly.

Figure legends you can use immediately

For the sweep figure:

Parameter sensitivity for highly variable genes and principal components. We tested multiple HVG and PC settings to identify the smallest dimensionality that preserved major placental lineages, retained infection/time-associated local structure, and improved donor mixing after Harmony correction. Preferred settings were those that maintained interpretable biological structure while avoiding over-correction or fragmentation.

For the final chosen setting:

Integration sensitivity at selected dimensionality. PCA was computed using the selected HVG set, followed by Harmony correction using donor identity as the batch variable. UMAPs were inspected for preservation of cell-type structure, improved donor mixing, and retention of infection/stage-associated organization. This setting was selected because it balanced cross-donor alignment with preservation of biologically meaningful heterogeneity.

Two small edits I would make later

First, once the sweep finishes, add one more summary table ranking settings by a composite score, for example:

high Harmony donor mixing

high Harmony cell-type purity

moderate condition retention

penalize obvious over-correction

Second, if you want a stronger paper figure, add one “late-PC interpretation” panel using DimHeatmap on a few boundary PCs to show that later PCs are either still biological or mostly weak/noisy. Seurat exposes those PCA inspection utilities directly.

> run_harmony_compat <- function(seu_obj, batch_col, dims = 1:30, reduction_save = "harmony") {
+   fn <- get("RunHarmony", envir = asNamespace("harmony"))
+   fn_formals <- names(formals(fn))
+   
+   args <- list(
+     object = seu_obj,
+     group.by.vars = batch_col,
+     verbose = FALSE
+   )
+   
+   if ("reduction" %in% fn_formals) {
+     args$reduction <- "pca"
+   } else if ("reduction.use" %in% fn_formals) {
+     args$reduction.use <- "pca"
+   }
+   
+   if ("dims.use" %in% fn_formals) args$dims.use <- dims
+   if ("assay.use" %in% fn_formals) args$assay.use <- "RNA"
+   if ("reduction.save" %in% fn_formals) args$reduction.save <- reduction_save
+   
+   do.call(fn, args)
+ }
> 
> safe_dimplot <- function(seu_obj, reduction, group_by, title_txt) {
+   if (!reduction %in% names(seu_obj@reductions)) return(NULL)
+   if (!group_by %in% colnames(seu_obj@meta.data)) return(NULL)
+   
+   DimPlot(seu_obj, reduction = reduction, group.by = group_by, raster = TRUE) +
+     ggtitle(title_txt)
+ }
> 
> save_if_not_null <- function(path, p, w = 10, h = 8) {
+   if (!is.null(p)) save_plot(path, p, w = w, h = h)
+ }
> 
> downsample_stratified <- function(seu_obj, max_cells = 30000, seed = 42) {
+   n <- ncol(seu_obj)
+   if (n <= max_cells) return(seu_obj)
+   
+   set.seed(seed)
+   md <- seu_obj@meta.data
+   
+   key <- if (all(c(CFG$cols$cell_type, CFG$cols$donor_id) %in% colnames(md))) {
+     paste(md[[CFG$cols$cell_type]], md[[CFG$cols$donor_id]], sep = "__")
+   } else {
+     rep("all", n)
+   }
+   
+   idx_by_group <- split(seq_len(n), key)
+   group_sizes <- vapply(idx_by_group, length, integer(1))
+   
+   target <- round(group_sizes / sum(group_sizes) * max_cells)
+   target[target == 0] <- 1L
+   target <- pmin(target, group_sizes)
+   
+   diff_n <- sum(target) - max_cells
+   if (diff_n > 0) {
+     reducible <- which(target > 1)
+     while (diff_n > 0 && length(reducible) > 0) {
+       j <- sample(reducible, 1)
+       target[j] <- target[j] - 1L
+       diff_n <- diff_n - 1L
+       reducible <- which(target > 1)
+     }
+   } else if (diff_n < 0) {
+     expandable <- which(target < group_sizes)
+     while (diff_n < 0 && length(expandable) > 0) {
+       j <- sample(expandable, 1)
+       target[j] <- target[j] + 1L
+       diff_n <- diff_n + 1L
+       expandable <- which(target < group_sizes)
+     }
+   }
+   
+   keep <- unlist(
+     Map(function(ix, k) sample(ix, size = k), idx_by_group, target),
+     use.names = FALSE
+   )
+   
+   subset(seu_obj, cells = colnames(seu_obj)[sort(keep)])
+ }
> 
> neighbor_purity <- function(emb, labels, k = 15) {
+   # emb: matrix cells x dims
+   # labels: vector
+   if (nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)
+   
+   d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
+   diag(d) <- Inf
+   nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])
+   
+   if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)
+   
+   pur <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
+     mean(labels[nn[, i]] == labels[i], na.rm = TRUE)
+   })
+   mean(pur, na.rm = TRUE)
+ }
> 
> mixing_score <- function(emb, batch, k = 15) {
+   # higher = more donor mixing
+   if (nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)
+   
+   d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
+   diag(d) <- Inf
+   nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])
+   
+   if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)
+   
+   mix <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
+     mean(batch[nn[, i]] != batch[i], na.rm = TRUE)
+   })
+   mean(mix, na.rm = TRUE)
+ }
> 
> condition_neighbor_enrichment <- function(emb, cond, k = 15) {
+   # higher = local condition coherence
+   if (length(unique(cond)) < 2 || nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)
+   
+   d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
+   diag(d) <- Inf
+   nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])
+   
+   if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)
+   
+   score <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
+     mean(cond[nn[, i]] == cond[i], na.rm = TRUE)
+   })
+   mean(score, na.rm = TRUE)
+ }
> 
> prep_pca <- function(obj, nfeatures, npcs = 60) {
+   DefaultAssay(obj) <- "RNA"
+   obj <- NormalizeData(obj, verbose = FALSE)
+   obj <- FindVariableFeatures(obj, nfeatures = nfeatures, verbose = FALSE)
+   obj <- ScaleData(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), verbose = FALSE)
+   obj <- RunPCA(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), npcs = npcs, verbose = FALSE)
+   obj
+ }
> 
> pc_var_table <- function(seu_obj) {
+   stdev <- seu_obj[["pca"]]@stdev
+   data.frame(
+     PC = seq_along(stdev),
+     stdev = stdev,
+     var_explained = (stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2),
+     cumvar = cumsum((stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2))
+   )
+ }
>

Thought for 33s

Yep — and the good news is the new error is much more straightforward than the first one.

What broke this time

The key failure is:

Error in `object[[reduction]]`:
! ‘harmony_4000_40’ not found in this Seurat object

That means Harmony ran, but it did not save the reduction under the custom name harmony_4000_40.

Why this happened:

your wrapper checks formals() on RunHarmony

but with S3/generic dispatch, that is not a reliable way to detect whether reduction.save is supported

so Harmony likely saved the reduction as the default "harmony" instead of "harmony_4000_40"

That matches Harmony’s documented Seurat method, where reduction.save is the argument that controls the slot name.

Fastest fix

Because each loop starts with:

tmp <- obj

you do not need unique Harmony reduction names at all.

Just use the default "harmony" every time.

Replace this whole block:

if (requireNamespace("harmony", quietly = TRUE)) {
  harm_name <- paste0("harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc)

  tmp <- run_harmony_compat(
    seu_obj = tmp,
    batch_col = batch_col,
    dims = 1:n_pc,
    reduction_save = harm_name
  )

  tmp <- RunUMAP(
    tmp,
    dims = 1:n_pc,
    reduction = harm_name,
    reduction.name = paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc),
    n.neighbors = 30,
    min.dist = 0.3,
    verbose = FALSE
  )
}

with this:

if (requireNamespace("harmony", quietly = TRUE)) {
  tmp <- harmony::RunHarmony(
    object = tmp,
    group.by.vars = batch_col,
    reduction.use = "pca",
    dims.use = 1:n_pc,
    reduction.save = "harmony",
    verbose = FALSE
  )

  tmp <- RunUMAP(
    tmp,
    dims = 1:n_pc,
    reduction = "harmony",
    reduction.name = paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc),
    n.neighbors = 30,
    min.dist = 0.3,
    verbose = FALSE
  )
}

That should eliminate the harmony_4000_40 not found problem.

Second problem: std::bad_alloc at 2000 HVGs

This part:

Error: std::bad_alloc
Called from: SparseRowVar2(...)

is happening during FindVariableFeatures(), not because 2000 is biologically wrong, but because the loop is keeping too much around in memory while repeatedly creating large Seurat objects. FindVariableFeatures() identifies variable genes by modeling mean–variance behavior, and ElbowPlot() is the lighter-weight way to judge PCs, whereas JackStraw() is explicitly the heavier formal test.

So yes: you absolutely can process one setting, save outputs, then remove objects and run garbage collection. That is fine practice here. gc() is literally R’s garbage collection mechanism, and using rm() plus gc() inside big loops is a normal way to control memory pressure in large workflows.

Your reduced grid is a good idea

Yes — I would narrow it now to:

hvg_grid <- c(3000, 4000, 5000)
pc_grid  <- c(30, 40, 50)

That is a much more realistic first pass for your dataset.

Best way to keep memory under control
1. Only keep one big Seurat object at a time inside the loop

At the end of each n_hvg loop, remove all large temporary objects:

rm(obj, tmp, p_elbow, p_vf, p1, p2, p3, p4, h1, h2, h3, h4, panel, hpanel, pca_tbl)
gc()

Wrap that safely like this:

rm(list = intersect(
  c("obj","tmp","p_elbow","p_vf","p1","p2","p3","p4","h1","h2","h3","h4","panel","hpanel","pca_tbl"),
  ls()
))
gc()
2. Remove JackStraw for now

JackStraw is much slower/heavier than ElbowPlot, and Seurat explicitly notes the elbow is much faster and often corresponds well to significant dimensions.

For now, comment out:

# js_obj <- prep_pca(seu_js, nfeatures = n_hvg, npcs = max(pc_grid))
# js_obj <- JackStraw(js_obj, dims = max(pc_grid), num.replicate = 100, verbose = FALSE)
# js_obj <- ScoreJackStraw(js_obj, dims = 1:max(pc_grid))
# p_js <- JackStrawPlot(js_obj, dims = 1:20) + ...
# save_plot(...)
# rm(js_obj, p_js)
# gc()

Do the HVG/PC sweep first. Then, if needed, run JackStraw only for the final 1–2 candidate settings on the 30k subset.

3. Clear old reductions before rerunning PCA inside prep_pca

Your warning:

Warning: Number of dimensions changing from 50 to 60

means you were reusing an object that already had PCA info. Not fatal, but messy.

Change prep_pca() to start from a trimmed copy:

prep_pca <- function(obj, nfeatures, npcs = 50) {
  DefaultAssay(obj) <- "RNA"

  # remove old reductions/graphs to keep object lighter
  obj@reductions <- list()
  obj@graphs <- list()
  obj@neighbors <- list()

  obj <- NormalizeData(obj, verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- FindVariableFeatures(obj, nfeatures = nfeatures, verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- ScaleData(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- RunPCA(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), npcs = npcs, verbose = FALSE)
  obj
}
4. Keep only what you need in the working object

Seurat has DietSeurat() specifically to slim objects by dropping reductions, graphs, and other components you do not need.

For example, right after loading:

seu <- DietSeurat(
  seu,
  assays = "RNA",
  layers = c("counts", "data"),
  dimreducs = NULL,
  graphs = NULL,
  misc = TRUE
)

I would not drop counts or normalized data, but dropping old reductions/graphs is reasonable for this sweep.

  object = tmp,

Then at the end of each inner loop:

rm(list = intersect(
  c("tmp","p1","p2","p3","p4","h1","h2","h3","h4","panel","hpanel"),
  ls()
))
gc()

And at the end of each outer loop:

rm(list = intersect(c("obj","p_elbow","p_vf","pca_tbl"), ls()))
gc()
One more improvement

Your metric functions currently do:

d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))

That is very memory expensive on tens of thousands of cells because it creates a full cell-by-cell distance matrix.

That may become your next bottleneck.

For now, since you are already generating UMAP panels, I would:

keep the plots

write the PCA variance table

postpone those neighbor-based metrics until we switch them to an approximate nearest-neighbor method

Otherwise the next crash may come from dist().

My recommendation for the next run

Restart R session

Use:

hvg_grid <- c(3000, 4000, 5000)
pc_grid  <- c(30, 40, 50)

Remove JackStraw for now

Use "harmony" as the reduction name every time

Add rm() + gc() after each loop

Skip the distance-matrix metrics for this run if memory still spikes

source("R/helpers_io.R")

suppressPackageStartupMessages({
  library(Seurat)
  library(dplyr)
  library(ggplot2)
  library(qs)
  library(patchwork)
})

# -----------------------------
# SETTINGS
# -----------------------------
log_file <- file.path(CFG$dirs$logs, "pipeline.log")
out_tbl  <- file.path(CFG$dirs$tables, "integration_param_sweep_summary.csv")

# Main grid to test
hvg_grid <- c(2000, 3000, 4000, 5000)
pc_grid  <- c(20, 30, 40, 50, 60)

# Optional subset for heavy formal diagnostics
jackstraw_cells <- 30000
seed <- 42

# -----------------------------
# HELPERS
# -----------------------------
run_harmony_compat <- function(seu_obj, batch_col, dims = 1:30, reduction_save = "harmony") {
  fn <- get("RunHarmony", envir = asNamespace("harmony"))
  fn_formals <- names(formals(fn))
  
  args <- list(
    object = seu_obj,
    group.by.vars = batch_col,
    verbose = FALSE
  )
  
  if ("reduction" %in% fn_formals) {
    args$reduction <- "pca"
  } else if ("reduction.use" %in% fn_formals) {
    args$reduction.use <- "pca"
  }
  
  if ("dims.use" %in% fn_formals) args$dims.use <- dims
  if ("assay.use" %in% fn_formals) args$assay.use <- "RNA"
  if ("reduction.save" %in% fn_formals) args$reduction.save <- reduction_save
  
  do.call(fn, args)
}

safe_dimplot <- function(seu_obj, reduction, group_by, title_txt) {
  if (!reduction %in% names(seu_obj@reductions)) return(NULL)
  if (!group_by %in% colnames(seu_obj@meta.data)) return(NULL)
  
  DimPlot(seu_obj, reduction = reduction, group.by = group_by, raster = TRUE) +
    ggtitle(title_txt)
}

save_if_not_null <- function(path, p, w = 10, h = 8) {
  if (!is.null(p)) save_plot(path, p, w = w, h = h)
}

downsample_stratified <- function(seu_obj, max_cells = 30000, seed = 42) {
  n <- ncol(seu_obj)
  if (n <= max_cells) return(seu_obj)
  
  set.seed(seed)
  md <- seu_obj@meta.data
  
  key <- if (all(c(CFG$cols$cell_type, CFG$cols$donor_id) %in% colnames(md))) {
    paste(md[[CFG$cols$cell_type]], md[[CFG$cols$donor_id]], sep = "__")
  } else {
    rep("all", n)
  }
  
  idx_by_group <- split(seq_len(n), key)
  group_sizes <- vapply(idx_by_group, length, integer(1))
  
  target <- round(group_sizes / sum(group_sizes) * max_cells)
  target[target == 0] <- 1L
  target <- pmin(target, group_sizes)
  
  diff_n <- sum(target) - max_cells
  if (diff_n > 0) {
    reducible <- which(target > 1)
    while (diff_n > 0 && length(reducible) > 0) {
      j <- sample(reducible, 1)
      target[j] <- target[j] - 1L
      diff_n <- diff_n - 1L
      reducible <- which(target > 1)
    }
  } else if (diff_n < 0) {
    expandable <- which(target < group_sizes)
    while (diff_n < 0 && length(expandable) > 0) {
      j <- sample(expandable, 1)
      target[j] <- target[j] + 1L
      diff_n <- diff_n + 1L
      expandable <- which(target < group_sizes)
    }
  }
  
  keep <- unlist(
    Map(function(ix, k) sample(ix, size = k), idx_by_group, target),
    use.names = FALSE
  )
  
  subset(seu_obj, cells = colnames(seu_obj)[sort(keep)])
}

neighbor_purity <- function(emb, labels, k = 15) {
  # emb: matrix cells x dims
  # labels: vector
  if (nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)
  
  d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
  diag(d) <- Inf
  nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])
  
  if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)
  
  pur <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
    mean(labels[nn[, i]] == labels[i], na.rm = TRUE)
  })
  mean(pur, na.rm = TRUE)
}

mixing_score <- function(emb, batch, k = 15) {
  # higher = more donor mixing
  if (nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)
  
  d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
  diag(d) <- Inf
  nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])
  
  if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)
  
  mix <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
    mean(batch[nn[, i]] != batch[i], na.rm = TRUE)
  })
  mean(mix, na.rm = TRUE)
}

condition_neighbor_enrichment <- function(emb, cond, k = 15) {
  # higher = local condition coherence
  if (length(unique(cond)) < 2 || nrow(emb) < (k + 1)) return(NA_real_)
  
  d <- as.matrix(dist(emb))
  diag(d) <- Inf
  nn <- apply(d, 1, function(x) order(x)[1:k])
  
  if (is.vector(nn)) nn <- matrix(nn, nrow = 1)
  
  score <- sapply(seq_len(nrow(emb)), function(i) {
    mean(cond[nn[, i]] == cond[i], na.rm = TRUE)
  })
  mean(score, na.rm = TRUE)
}

prep_pca <- function(obj, nfeatures, npcs = 60) {
  DefaultAssay(obj) <- "RNA"
  obj <- NormalizeData(obj, verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- FindVariableFeatures(obj, nfeatures = nfeatures, verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- ScaleData(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- RunPCA(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), npcs = npcs, verbose = FALSE)
  obj
}

pc_var_table <- function(seu_obj) {
  stdev <- seu_obj[["pca"]]@stdev
  data.frame(
    PC = seq_along(stdev),
    stdev = stdev,
    var_explained = (stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2),
    cumvar = cumsum((stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2))
  )
}

# -----------------------------
# LOAD OBJECT
# -----------------------------
log_msg("07b_parameter_sensitivity starting.", log_file = log_file)

seu <- qs::qread(file.path(CFG$dirs$objects, "seu_with_scores.qs"))
DefaultAssay(seu) <- "RNA"

batch_col <- CFG$cols$donor_id
if (!batch_col %in% colnames(seu@meta.data)) {
  stop("Missing donor/batch column: ", batch_col)
}

if (!"condition" %in% colnames(seu@meta.data) &&
    all(c(CFG$cols$infection, CFG$cols$hpi) %in% colnames(seu@meta.data))) {
  seu$condition <- paste0(seu[[CFG$cols$infection]][,1], "_", seu[[CFG$cols$hpi]][,1])
}

# representative subset for formal/fast diagnostics if needed
seu_js <- downsample_stratified(seu, max_cells = jackstraw_cells, seed = seed)

summary_rows <- list()

# -----------------------------

for (n_hvg in hvg_grid) {
  log_msg("Starting HVG setting: ", n_hvg, log_file = log_file)
  
  obj <- prep_pca(seu, nfeatures = n_hvg, npcs = max(pc_grid))
  pca_tbl <- pc_var_table(obj)
  
  # Save elbow plot and variance table for each HVG setting
  p_elbow <- ElbowPlot(obj, ndims = max(pc_grid), reduction = "pca") +
    ggtitle(paste0("ElbowPlot | HVGs=", n_hvg))
  save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_Elbow_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
            p_elbow, w = 9, h = 6)
  
  write.csv(
    pca_tbl,
    file.path(CFG$dirs$tables, paste0("PCA_variance_HVG", n_hvg, ".csv")),
    row.names = FALSE
  )
  
  # Optional variable feature plot
  p_vf <- VariableFeaturePlot(obj) +
    ggtitle(paste0("VariableFeaturePlot | HVGs=", n_hvg))
  save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_VariableFeatures_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
            p_vf, w = 9, h = 6)
  
  for (n_pc in pc_grid) {
    log_msg("Running HVG=", n_hvg, " | PCs=", n_pc, log_file = log_file)
    
    tmp <- obj
    
    # Non-integrated UMAP
    tmp <- RunUMAP(
      tmp,
      dims = 1:n_pc,
      reduction = "pca",
      reduction.name = paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc),
      n.neighbors = 30,
      min.dist = 0.3,
      verbose = FALSE
    )
    
    # Harmony + Harmony UMAP
    if (requireNamespace("harmony", quietly = TRUE)) {
      harm_name <- paste0("harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc)
      
      tmp <- run_harmony_compat(
        seu_obj = tmp,
        batch_col = batch_col,
        dims = 1:n_pc,
        reduction_save = harm_name
      )
      
      tmp <- RunUMAP(
        tmp,
        dims = 1:n_pc,
        reduction = harm_name,
        reduction.name = paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc),
        n.neighbors = 30,
        min.dist = 0.3,
        verbose = FALSE
      )
    }
    
    # Figure panel for this combination
    p1 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$cell_type,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | cell type | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p2 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), batch_col,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | donor | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p3 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$infection,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | infection | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p4 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_rna_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), "condition",
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | condition | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    
    if (!is.null(p1) && !is.null(p2) && !is.null(p3) && !is.null(p4)) {
      panel <- (p1 | p2) / (p3 | p4)
      save_plot(
        file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_RNA_HVG", n_hvg, "_PC", n_pc, ".pdf")),
        panel, w = 16, h = 12
      )
    }
    
    if (paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc) %in% names(tmp@reductions)) {
      h1 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$cell_type,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | cell type | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h2 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), batch_col,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | donor | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h3 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), CFG$cols$infection,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | infection | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h4 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, paste0("umap_harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc), "condition",
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | condition | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      
      if (!is.null(h1) && !is.null(h2) && !is.null(h3) && !is.null(h4)) {
        hpanel <- (h1 | h2) / (h3 | h4)
        save_plot(
          file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_Harmony_HVG", n_hvg, "_PC", n_pc, ".pdf")),
          hpanel, w = 16, h = 12
        )
      }
    }
    
    # Quantitative metrics on embeddings
    emb_pca <- Embeddings(tmp, "pca")[, 1:n_pc, drop = FALSE]
    ct_lab <- tmp@meta.data[[CFG$cols$cell_type]]
    donor_lab <- tmp@meta.data[[batch_col]]
    cond_lab <- if ("condition" %in% colnames(tmp@meta.data)) tmp@meta.data$condition else rep(NA, ncol(tmp))
    
    pca_celltype_purity <- neighbor_purity(emb_pca, ct_lab, k = 15)
    pca_donor_mixing <- mixing_score(emb_pca, donor_lab, k = 15)
    pca_condition_local <- condition_neighbor_enrichment(emb_pca, cond_lab, k = 15)
    
    harm_celltype_purity <- NA_real_
    harm_donor_mixing <- NA_real_
    harm_condition_local <- NA_real_
    
    harm_name <- paste0("harmony_", n_hvg, "_", n_pc)
    if (harm_name %in% names(tmp@reductions)) {
      emb_h <- Embeddings(tmp, harm_name)[, 1:n_pc, drop = FALSE]
      harm_celltype_purity <- neighbor_purity(emb_h, ct_lab, k = 15)
      harm_donor_mixing <- mixing_score(emb_h, donor_lab, k = 15)
      harm_condition_local <- condition_neighbor_enrichment(emb_h, cond_lab, k = 15)
    }
    
    summary_rows[[length(summary_rows) + 1]] <- data.frame(
      n_cells = ncol(tmp),
      hvg = n_hvg,
      pcs = n_pc,
      pca_var_pc1_10 = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(10, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_var_pc1_20 = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(20, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_var_pc1_n = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(n_pc, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_celltype_purity = pca_celltype_purity,
      pca_donor_mixing = pca_donor_mixing,
      pca_condition_local = pca_condition_local,
      harmony_celltype_purity = harm_celltype_purity,
      harmony_donor_mixing = harm_donor_mixing,
      harmony_condition_local = harm_condition_local
    )
  }
  
  # Optional JackStraw on subset only for this HVG setting
  log_msg("Running JackStraw subset diagnostic for HVG=", n_hvg, log_file = log_file)
  js_obj <- prep_pca(seu_js, nfeatures = n_hvg, npcs = max(pc_grid))
  js_obj <- JackStraw(js_obj, dims = max(pc_grid), num.replicate = 100, verbose = FALSE)
  js_obj <- ScoreJackStraw(js_obj, dims = 1:max(pc_grid))
  
  p_js <- JackStrawPlot(js_obj, dims = 1:20) +
    ggtitle(paste0("JackStraw subset | HVGs=", n_hvg))
  save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_JackStraw_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
            p_js, w = 12, h = 8)
}

summary_df <- bind_rows(summary_rows)
write.csv(summary_df, out_tbl, row.names = FALSE)

# Summary score plots
p_mix <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = pcs, y = harmony_donor_mixing, color = factor(hvg), group = hvg)) +
  geom_line() + geom_point() +
  labs(title = "Harmony donor mixing across HVG/PC settings", color = "HVGs") +
  theme_bw()

p_purity <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = pcs, y = harmony_celltype_purity, color = factor(hvg), group = hvg)) +
  geom_line() + geom_point() +
  labs(title = "Harmony cell-type purity across HVG/PC settings", color = "HVGs") +
  theme_bw()

p_cond <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = pcs, y = harmony_condition_local, color = factor(hvg), group = hvg)) +
  geom_line() + geom_point() +
  labs(title = "Harmony condition-locality across HVG/PC settings", color = "HVGs") +
  theme_bw()

save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_donor_mixing.pdf"), p_mix, w = 10, h = 7)
save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_celltype_purity.pdf"), p_purity, w = 10, h = 7)
save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_condition_locality.pdf"), p_cond, w = 10, h = 7)

write_legend(
  "FigParam", "Parameter sensitivity for HVGs and PCs",
  hypothesis = "The chosen dimensionality settings should preserve major placental lineages and infection/time-associated biology while minimizing donor-driven structure after batch correction.",
  methods = paste(
    "Tested HVGs =", paste(hvg_grid, collapse = ","),
    "; tested PCs =", paste(pc_grid, collapse = ","),
    ". For each setting, we ran PCA, non-integrated UMAP, Harmony integration by donor, Harmony UMAP, and subset-based JackStraw diagnostics."
  ),
  readout = paste(
    "Preferred settings show strong cell-type coherence, improved donor mixing after Harmony,",
    "and retention of condition-associated local structure without evidence of over-correction."
  ),
  interpretation_template = paste(
    "- Choose the smallest PC range that stabilizes biological structure.",
    "\n- Favor HVG settings that preserve rare/important populations without fragmenting embeddings.",
    "\n- If donor mixing improves but infection/stage structure collapses, integration is likely too aggressive.",
    "\n- If larger HVG settings do not improve biological resolution, prefer the simpler setting."
  ),
  outfile = file.path(CFG$dirs$legends, "FigParam_legend.md")
)

Thought for 24s

Absolutely — below is a rewritten, leaner 07b_parameter_sensitivity.R that does what you asked:

narrows to HVG = 3000, 4000, 5000

narrows to PC = 30, 40, 50

comments out JackStraw for now

keeps ElbowPlot

adds a simple automatic elbow suggestion

saves intermediate objects with qs

removes large temp objects and runs gc() to keep memory down

uses default Harmony reduction name "harmony" to avoid the slot-name bug

adds comments explaining why each step exists for your project

A couple of earlier uploaded files have expired on my side, so if you want me to inspect those again later, re-upload them.

Seurat documents FindVariableFeatures() with default selection.method = "vst" and default nfeatures = 2000, but that is a default rather than a rule; the function is meant to identify genes that are unusually variable relative to their mean expression. Seurat also notes that ElbowPlot() is a fast way to find a reasonable PC cutoff and is much faster than JackStraw, which is why deferring JackStraw here is a good call. Harmony’s Seurat method expects PCA already computed and supports dims.use plus reduction.save, so using the standard "harmony" reduction name is clean and robust. DietSeurat() is also explicitly intended to slim objects by removing reductions/graphs you do not need.

Rewritten script
source("R/config.R")
source("R/helpers_io.R")

suppressPackageStartupMessages({
  library(Seurat)
  library(dplyr)
  library(ggplot2)
  library(qs)
  library(patchwork)
})

# =========================================================
# 07b_parameter_sensitivity.R
#
# PURPOSE
# -------
# Test a small, biologically reasonable grid of:
#   - HVGs: 3000, 4000, 5000
#   - PCs : 30, 40, 50
#
# Why this exists:
#   1) Placenta is highly heterogeneous, so 2000 HVGs may be too conservative.
#   2) We want an evidence-based choice of dimensionality for manuscript-quality work.
#   3) We want to preserve biologically meaningful structure:
#        - major placental cell types
#        - infection/time patterns
#        - donor correction without over-correction
#        - FIB2 / stromal / trophoblast / immune structure
#
# DESIGN CHOICES
# --------------
# - Keep ElbowPlot diagnostics
# - Skip JackStraw for now (computationally expensive)
# - Save intermediate objects with qs for reproducibility and recovery
# - Remove temporary objects and run gc() inside loops to reduce memory pressure
# - Use default Harmony reduction name "harmony" within each loop
#   because each loop starts from a fresh object
# =========================================================

# -----------------------------
# SETTINGS
# -----------------------------
log_file <- file.path(CFG$dirs$logs, "pipeline.log")
out_tbl  <- file.path(CFG$dirs$tables, "integration_param_sweep_summary.csv")
obj_dir  <- file.path(CFG$dirs$objects, "parameter_sweep")
dir.create(obj_dir, showWarnings = FALSE, recursive = TRUE)

# Reduced grid: practical + biologically sensible first pass
hvg_grid <- c(3000, 4000, 5000)
pc_grid  <- c(30, 40, 50)

seed <- 42

# Save per-combination objects?
# TRUE = very reproducible, but more disk usage
# FALSE = lighter on disk
save_combo_objects <- TRUE

# -----------------------------
# HELPERS
# -----------------------------

safe_dimplot <- function(seu_obj, reduction, group_by, title_txt) {
  if (!reduction %in% names(seu_obj@reductions)) return(NULL)
  if (!group_by %in% colnames(seu_obj@meta.data)) return(NULL)

  DimPlot(seu_obj, reduction = reduction, group.by = group_by, raster = TRUE) +
    ggtitle(title_txt)
}

save_if_not_null <- function(path, p, w = 10, h = 8) {
  if (!is.null(p)) save_plot(path, p, w = w, h = h)
}

# Simple elbow suggestion:
# returns the first PC after which marginal gain becomes small
# This is a heuristic, not a substitute for biological review.
suggest_elbow_pc <- function(seu_obj, min_pc = 10, max_pc = 50, rel_drop_thresh = 0.10) {
  stdev <- seu_obj[["pca"]]@stdev
  max_pc <- min(max_pc, length(stdev))

  if (max_pc < (min_pc + 2)) return(NA_integer_)

  vars <- stdev[1:max_pc]^2
  deltas <- -diff(vars)  # variance drop from PC_i to PC_{i+1}

  # relative drop compared with the first drop
  rel <- deltas / deltas[1]

  # first PC where the incremental drop becomes "small"
  idx <- which(seq_along(rel) >= min_pc & rel < rel_drop_thresh)[1]

  if (is.na(idx)) {
    return(max_pc)
  } else {
    return(idx)
  }
}

prep_pca <- function(obj, nfeatures, npcs = 50) {
  DefaultAssay(obj) <- "RNA"

  # Drop old reductions/graphs to keep the working copy lighter.
  # Seurat provides DietSeurat specifically for slimming objects. 
  obj <- DietSeurat(
    object = obj,
    assays = "RNA",
    layers = c("counts", "data"),
    dimreducs = NULL,
    graphs = NULL,
    misc = TRUE
  )

  obj <- NormalizeData(obj, verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- FindVariableFeatures(
    obj,
    selection.method = "vst",
    nfeatures = nfeatures,
    verbose = FALSE
  )
  obj <- ScaleData(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), verbose = FALSE)
  obj <- RunPCA(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), npcs = npcs, verbose = FALSE)

  obj
}

pc_var_table <- function(seu_obj) {
  stdev <- seu_obj[["pca"]]@stdev
  data.frame(
    PC = seq_along(stdev),
    stdev = stdev,
    var_explained = (stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2),
    cumvar = cumsum((stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2))
  )
}

run_harmony_safe <- function(seu_obj, batch_col, dims_use) {
  # Harmony documentation indicates PCA must already exist.
  # We use the default reduction.save = "harmony" within each fresh loop object.
  harmony::RunHarmony(
    object = seu_obj,
    group.by.vars = batch_col,
    reduction = "pca",
    dims.use = dims_use,
    assay.use = "RNA",
    reduction.save = "harmony",
    verbose = FALSE
  )
}

cleanup_big_objects <- function() {
  gc(verbose = FALSE)
}

# -----------------------------
# LOAD OBJECT
# -----------------------------
log_msg("07b_parameter_sensitivity starting.", log_file = log_file)

seu <- qs::qread(file.path(CFG$dirs$objects, "seu_with_scores.qs"))
DefaultAssay(seu) <- "RNA"

batch_col <- CFG$cols$donor_id
if (!batch_col %in% colnames(seu@meta.data)) {
  stop("Missing donor/batch column: ", batch_col)
}

# Build combined condition label if absent.
if (!"condition" %in% colnames(seu@meta.data) &&
    all(c(CFG$cols$infection, CFG$cols$hpi) %in% colnames(seu@meta.data))) {
  seu$condition <- paste0(seu[[CFG$cols$infection]][,1], "_", seu[[CFG$cols$hpi]][,1])
}

summary_rows <- list()

# Save the base object metadata snapshot for reproducibility
qs::qsave(
  x = seu,
  file = file.path(obj_dir, "base_input_object_for_parameter_sweep.qs")
)

# -----------------------------
# PARAMETER SWEEP
# -----------------------------
for (n_hvg in hvg_grid) {

  log_msg("Starting HVG setting: ", n_hvg, log_file = log_file)

  # Fresh working copy for this HVG setting
  obj <- tryCatch(
    prep_pca(seu, nfeatures = n_hvg, npcs = max(pc_grid)),
    error = function(e) {
      log_msg("prep_pca failed for HVG=", n_hvg, " :: ", conditionMessage(e), log_file = log_file)
      stop(e)
    }
  )

  pca_tbl <- pc_var_table(obj)
  elbow_pc_auto <- suggest_elbow_pc(obj, min_pc = 10, max_pc = max(pc_grid), rel_drop_thresh = 0.10)

  # Save PCA variance table
  pca_tbl$hvg <- n_hvg
  pca_tbl$auto_elbow_pc <- elbow_pc_auto

  write.csv(
    pca_tbl,
    file.path(CFG$dirs$tables, paste0("PCA_variance_HVG", n_hvg, ".csv")),
    row.names = FALSE
  )

  # Save HVG-level object after PCA
  qs::qsave(
    x = obj,
    file = file.path(obj_dir, paste0("seu_PCA_HVG", n_hvg, ".qs"))
  )

  # Elbow plot with automatic suggestion annotated
  p_elbow <- ElbowPlot(obj, ndims = max(pc_grid), reduction = "pca") +
    geom_vline(xintercept = elbow_pc_auto, linetype = "dashed") +
    ggtitle(paste0("ElbowPlot | HVGs=", n_hvg, " | auto elbow ~ PC ", elbow_pc_auto))

  save_plot(
    file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_Elbow_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
    p_elbow, w = 9, h = 6
  )

  # Variable feature plot
  p_vf <- VariableFeaturePlot(obj) +
    ggtitle(paste0("VariableFeaturePlot | HVGs=", n_hvg))

  save_plot(
    file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_VariableFeatures_HVG", n_hvg, ".pdf")),
    p_vf, w = 9, h = 6
  )

  # Per-PC loop
  for (n_pc in pc_grid) {

    log_msg("Running HVG=", n_hvg, " | PCs=", n_pc, log_file = log_file)

    # Fresh copy from the HVG-specific PCA object
    tmp <- obj

    # -----------------------------
    # Non-integrated UMAP
    # -----------------------------
    tmp <- RunUMAP(
      tmp,
      dims = 1:n_pc,
      reduction = "pca",
      reduction.name = "umap_rna",
      n.neighbors = 30,
      min.dist = 0.3,
      verbose = FALSE
    )

    # -----------------------------
    # Harmony + Harmony UMAP
    # -----------------------------
    if (requireNamespace("harmony", quietly = TRUE)) {
      tmp <- tryCatch(
        run_harmony_safe(tmp, batch_col = batch_col, dims_use = 1:n_pc),
        error = function(e) {
          log_msg("Harmony failed for HVG=", n_hvg, " | PC=", n_pc, " :: ", conditionMessage(e), log_file = log_file)
          tmp
        }
      )

      if ("harmony" %in% names(tmp@reductions)) {
        tmp <- RunUMAP(
          tmp,
          dims = 1:n_pc,
          reduction = "harmony",
          reduction.name = "umap_harmony",
          n.neighbors = 30,
          min.dist = 0.3,
          verbose = FALSE
        )
      }
    }

    # -----------------------------
    # Save object for this combination
    # -----------------------------
    if (isTRUE(save_combo_objects)) {
      qs::qsave(
        x = tmp,
        file = file.path(obj_dir, paste0("seu_HVG", n_hvg, "_PC", n_pc, ".qs"))
      )
    }

    # -----------------------------
    # RNA UMAP panel
    # -----------------------------
    p1 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_rna", CFG$cols$cell_type,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | cell type | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p2 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_rna", batch_col,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | donor | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p3 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_rna", CFG$cols$infection,
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | infection | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
    p4 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_rna", "condition",
                       paste0("RNA UMAP | condition | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))

    if (!is.null(p1) && !is.null(p2) && !is.null(p3) && !is.null(p4)) {
      panel <- (p1 | p2) / (p3 | p4)
      save_plot(
        file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_RNA_HVG", n_hvg, "_PC", n_pc, ".pdf")),
        panel, w = 16, h = 12
      )
    }

    # -----------------------------
    # Harmony UMAP panel
    # -----------------------------
    if ("umap_harmony" %in% names(tmp@reductions)) {
      h1 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_harmony", CFG$cols$cell_type,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | cell type | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h2 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_harmony", batch_col,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | donor | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h3 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_harmony", CFG$cols$infection,
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | infection | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))
      h4 <- safe_dimplot(tmp, "umap_harmony", "condition",
                         paste0("Harmony UMAP | condition | HVG=", n_hvg, " PC=", n_pc))

      if (!is.null(h1) && !is.null(h2) && !is.null(h3) && !is.null(h4)) {
        hpanel <- (h1 | h2) / (h3 | h4)
        save_plot(
          file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, paste0("FigParam_Harmony_HVG", n_hvg, "_PC", n_pc, ".pdf")),
          hpanel, w = 16, h = 12
        )
      }
    }

    # -----------------------------
    # Summary row
    # -----------------------------
    summary_rows[[length(summary_rows) + 1]] <- data.frame(
      n_cells = ncol(tmp),
      hvg = n_hvg,
      pcs = n_pc,
      auto_elbow_pc = elbow_pc_auto,
      pca_var_pc1_10 = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(10, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_var_pc1_20 = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(20, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      pca_var_pc1_n  = sum(pca_tbl$var_explained[1:min(n_pc, nrow(pca_tbl))]),
      harmony_success = "harmony" %in% names(tmp@reductions),
      stringsAsFactors = FALSE
    )

    # -----------------------------
    # Clean up large temp objects
    # -----------------------------
    rm(list = intersect(
      c("tmp", "p1", "p2", "p3", "p4", "panel", "h1", "h2", "h3", "h4", "hpanel"),
      ls()
    ))
    cleanup_big_objects()
  }

  # Clean HVG-level objects before next HVG
  rm(list = intersect(c("obj", "pca_tbl", "p_elbow", "p_vf", "elbow_pc_auto"), ls()))
  cleanup_big_objects()
}

# -----------------------------
# WRITE SUMMARY TABLE
# -----------------------------
summary_df <- bind_rows(summary_rows)
write.csv(summary_df, out_tbl, row.names = FALSE)

# Also save summary as qs
qs::qsave(summary_df, file.path(obj_dir, "integration_param_sweep_summary.qs"))

# -----------------------------
# SUMMARY PLOTS
# -----------------------------
p_var <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = pcs, y = pca_var_pc1_n, color = factor(hvg), group = hvg)) +
  geom_line() + geom_point() +
  labs(
    title = "Cumulative PCA variance explained across HVG/PC settings",
    x = "PCs used",
    y = "Cumulative variance explained",
    color = "HVGs"
  ) +
  theme_bw()

p_elbow_suggest <- ggplot(summary_df, aes(x = factor(hvg), y = auto_elbow_pc)) +
  geom_point(size = 3) +
  labs(
    title = "Automatic elbow suggestion by HVG setting",
    x = "HVGs",
    y = "Suggested elbow PC"
  ) +
  theme_bw()

save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_variance_explained.pdf"), p_var, w = 10, h = 7)
save_plot(file.path(CFG$dirs$figures, "FigParam_Summary_auto_elbow.pdf"), p_elbow_suggest, w = 8, h = 6)

# -----------------------------
# LEGEND
# -----------------------------
write_legend(
  "FigParam", "Parameter sensitivity for HVGs and PCs",
  hypothesis = paste(
    "The selected dimensionality should preserve major placental lineages, infection/time-associated biology,",
    "and donor-corrected structure without evidence of over-correction."
  ),
  methods = paste(
    "Tested HVGs =", paste(hvg_grid, collapse = ","),
    "; tested PCs =", paste(pc_grid, collapse = ","),
    ". For each HVG setting, PCA was computed, ElbowPlot and VariableFeaturePlot were saved,",
    "and non-integrated plus Harmony-corrected UMAPs were generated for each PC setting.",
    "Intermediate objects were saved with qs for reproducibility and recovery."
  ),
  readout = paste(
    "Preferred settings should preserve biologically expected structure across cell type, donor, infection, and condition overlays.",
    "Automatic elbow suggestions are heuristic only and should be interpreted together with the UMAP panels and biological coherence."
  ),
  interpretation_template = paste(
    "- Prefer the smallest PC setting that preserves stable biological structure.",
    "\n- Favor HVG settings that preserve rare or important populations without obvious fragmentation.",
    "\n- If donor correction improves but infection/time structure collapses, Harmony may be over-correcting.",
    "\n- If 4000 and 5000 perform similarly, the simpler or more stable setting may be preferable."
  ),
  outfile = file.path(CFG$dirs$legends, "FigParam_legend.md")
)

# -----------------------------
# OPTIONAL JACKSTRAW (DEFERRED)
# -----------------------------
# Intentionally skipped for now.
# Seurat documentation notes that ElbowPlot is much faster than JackStraw
# and often corresponds well with significant dimensions.
# If needed, run JackStraw later only on 1-2 finalist settings and on a subset.

log_msg("07b_parameter_sensitivity done.", log_file = log_file)
What changed and why

The main changes are:

1. Smaller grid

You asked for:

hvg_grid <- c(3000, 4000, 5000)
pc_grid  <- c(30, 40, 50)

That is a much better first-pass grid for this dataset.

2. JackStraw removed for now

That was the right move. Seurat explicitly says ElbowPlot() is much faster and often tracks the significant dimensions well.

3. Harmony naming simplified

I removed the custom Harmony reduction names and just use:

reduction.save = "harmony"

inside each fresh loop object. Harmony’s docs explicitly support reduction.save, but since you rebuild tmp every iteration, unique names are not necessary.

4. Memory trimming

Inside prep_pca(), I use DietSeurat() to remove reductions and graphs from the working copy before recomputing PCA. Seurat documents DietSeurat() as a way to keep only selected object components and to remove all dim reductions or graphs when set to NULL.

5. qs saving

This version saves:

the base input object for the sweep

each HVG-level PCA object

each HVG/PC combination object, if save_combo_objects <- TRUE

the final summary table as both CSV and QS

That is good practice here because it makes the sweep restartable and auditable.

6. Automatic elbow suggestion

I added a simple heuristic. It is useful, but it is not the final decision-maker. Use it as:

one hint

alongside ElbowPlot

alongside UMAP biological interpretability

What I would keep in your environment

After restarting R and running this script, you mostly only need:

seu

CFG

helper functions

final summary objects

The big temp objects from your screenshot like tmp, obj, seu_int, seu_js, and large plot objects are safe to remove once they are not needed.

My actual recommendation for your project

For now, I would expect the likely winner to be one of:

4000 HVGs + 40 PCs

4000 HVGs + 50 PCs

5000 HVGs + 40 PCs

Then you review:

ElbowPlot

RNA UMAPs

Harmony UMAPs

whether donor mixing improves without wiping infection/time structure

whether FIB2 and trophoblast-state structure remain coherent

If you want, next I can write a 07c_final_parameter_selection.R script that:

reads the sweep summary

locks in one chosen HVG/PC pair

saves one final integrated object

writes final figure legends for the manuscript.

It does not look like it is still running.

In your screenshot, the console has returned to a normal > prompt after:

[2026-03-11 13:30:00] Starting HVG setting: 3000

If the script were still actively running in that same console, you usually would not have the prompt back yet. So it looks like it either stopped immediately after logging that line, or only that block got sent and execution did not continue.

What did run is at least the earlier 4000 HVG pass, because you already produced:

FigParam_Elbow_HVG4000.pdf

FigParam_VariableFeatures_HVG4000.pdf

the Harmony UMAP outputs

So that part clearly executed.

What the existing outputs suggest

From the figures you uploaded, the earlier Harmony result looks biologically reasonable at a first pass:

Cell types are well separated in the Harmony UMAP, which is what you want for a major lineage sanity check.

Donors look fairly well mixed across the same structures, which suggests Harmony is reducing donor-driven segregation.

Infection labels are broadly mixed, which usually means infection is not dominating the whole manifold globally. That is not necessarily bad; for your project, I would expect infection effects to be more cell-type/state-specific rather than creating a full-dataset split.

So as a quick interpretation: the original 4000-feature Harmony run looks reasonable enough to keep as a candidate setting, not something I would throw out.

My read on the 4000-HVG candidate

The VariableFeaturePlot confirms that 4,000 genes were selected as variable out of 36,601 total, so that part worked as intended. The ElbowPlot was also created, and Seurat’s own documentation says the elbow often corresponds well to informative dimensions and is much faster than JackStraw, which supports your choice to use elbow-based review first.

Given your placenta heterogeneity, 4000 HVGs is still a strong candidate. I would keep it in the finalist set.

Why the newer sweep may have stopped

Most likely one of these happened:

Only part of the script got sent to the console.

It hit an error right after that log line, but the error is above the visible region.

It is waiting at a browser/debug prompt from a caught error somewhere.

The loop started, but a command was interrupted.

The easiest check is to scroll up just above that Starting HVG setting: 3000 line and look for:

Error:

Browse[1]>

Selection:

or any warning immediately after the loop began

What I would do next

Run just this in the console:

traceback()

If nothing useful shows, rerun the first outer-loop block manually:

n_hvg <- 3000
obj <- prep_pca(seu, nfeatures = n_hvg, npcs = max(pc_grid))

That will tell you immediately whether the failure is still at FindVariableFeatures, ScaleData, or RunPCA.

One small script tweak I recommend

Add explicit progress logging inside prep_pca() so you know exactly where it stops:

prep_pca <- function(obj, nfeatures, npcs = 50) {
  DefaultAssay(obj) <- "RNA"

  log_msg("DietSeurat start", log_file = log_file)
  obj <- DietSeurat(
    object = obj,
    assays = "RNA",
    layers = c("counts", "data"),
    dimreducs = NULL,
    graphs = NULL,
    misc = TRUE
  )

  log_msg("NormalizeData start", log_file = log_file)
  obj <- NormalizeData(obj, verbose = FALSE)

  log_msg(paste0("FindVariableFeatures start nfeatures=", nfeatures), log_file = log_file)
  obj <- FindVariableFeatures(
    obj,
    selection.method = "vst",
    nfeatures = nfeatures,
    verbose = FALSE
  )

  log_msg("ScaleData start", log_file = log_file)
  obj <- ScaleData(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), verbose = FALSE)

  log_msg(paste0("RunPCA start npcs=", npcs), log_file = log_file)
  obj <- RunPCA(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), npcs = npcs, verbose = FALSE)

  log_msg("prep_pca done", log_file = log_file)
  obj
}

That will make the pipeline log much more informative.

On the Harmony arguments

Using the default Harmony reduction name "harmony" inside each loop is the right approach. Harmony’s Seurat method supports reduction.save, and downstream Seurat analyses are expected to use reduction='harmony'.

My practical recommendation

I would proceed like this:

keep the original 4000 HVG result as a valid benchmark

debug the sweep at 3000 HVG manually first

if 3000 is unstable or memory-heavy, skip straight to:

4000 HVG + 30/40/50 PCs

5000 HVG + 30/40/50 PCs

That gives you a cleaner comparison around the setting that already appears to work.

and I’ll pinpoint exactly where it is stopping.

> save_if_not_null <- function(path, p, w = 10, h = 8) {
+   if (!is.null(p)) save_plot(path, p, w = w, h = h)
+ }
> # Simple elbow suggestion:
> # returns the first PC after which marginal gain becomes small
> # This is a heuristic, not a substitute for biological review.
> suggest_elbow_pc <- function(seu_obj, min_pc = 10, max_pc = 50, rel_drop_thresh = 0.10) {
+   stdev <- seu_obj[["pca"]]@stdev
+   max_pc <- min(max_pc, length(stdev))
+   
+   if (max_pc < (min_pc + 2)) return(NA_integer_)
+   
+   vars <- stdev[1:max_pc]^2
+   deltas <- -diff(vars)  # variance drop from PC_i to PC_{i+1}
+   
+   # relative drop compared with the first drop
+   rel <- deltas / deltas[1]
+   
+   # first PC where the incremental drop becomes "small"
+   idx <- which(seq_along(rel) >= min_pc & rel < rel_drop_thresh)[1]
+   
+   if (is.na(idx)) {
+     return(max_pc)
+   } else {
+     return(idx)
+   }
+ }
> prep_pca <- function(obj, nfeatures, npcs = 50) {
+   DefaultAssay(obj) <- "RNA"
+   
+   # Drop old reductions/graphs to keep the working copy lighter.
+   # Seurat provides DietSeurat specifically for slimming objects. 
+   obj <- DietSeurat(
+     object = obj,
+     assays = "RNA",
+     layers = c("counts", "data"),
+     dimreducs = NULL,
+     graphs = NULL,
+     misc = TRUE
+   )
+   
+   obj <- NormalizeData(obj, verbose = FALSE)
+   obj <- FindVariableFeatures(
+     obj,
+     selection.method = "vst",
+     nfeatures = nfeatures,
+     verbose = FALSE
+   )
+   obj <- ScaleData(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), verbose = FALSE)
+   obj <- RunPCA(obj, features = VariableFeatures(obj), npcs = npcs, verbose = FALSE)
+   
+   obj
+ }
> pc_var_table <- function(seu_obj) {
+   stdev <- seu_obj[["pca"]]@stdev
+   data.frame(
+     PC = seq_along(stdev),
+     stdev = stdev,
+     var_explained = (stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2),
+     cumvar = cumsum((stdev^2) / sum(stdev^2))
+   )
+ }
> run_harmony_safe <- function(seu_obj, batch_col, dims_use) {
+   # Harmony documentation indicates PCA must already exist.
+   # We use the default reduction.save = "harmony" within each fresh loop object.
+   harmony::RunHarmony(
+     object = seu_obj,
+     group.by.vars = batch_col,
+     reduction = "pca",
+     dims.use = dims_use,
+     assay.use = "RNA",
+     reduction.save = "harmony",
+     verbose = FALSE
+   )
+ }
> cleanup_big_objects <- function() {
+   gc(verbose = FALSE)
+ }
